```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Task: Kubernetes API Server Architecture and Extension Guide

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kubernetes--8c9c67c0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture and extension guide for the apiserver library with request-path flow and extension tradeoffs.

## Scope

Focus on the Kubernetes apiserver library subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

Server Composition\n4: \n5: The `kube-apiserver` binary is not one server, but a **server chain** of three distinct\n6: `GenericAPIServer` instances: the core Kubernetes API, API extensions (CRDs), and the aggregation\n7: layer.\n8: \n9: This composition is managed by a layered configuration system, starting with command-line\n10: flags parsed by `options` structs (e.g., `RecommendedOptions` in `pkg/server/options`), which\n11: populate a `Config` object that is then used to instantiate the `GenericAPIServer`\n12: instances.      1→# Kubernetes API Server Library: Architecture and Extension Guide
     2→
     3→## 1. Subsystem Overview
     4→
     5→The Kubernetes API server library (`k8s.io/apiserver`) is a reusable framework for building Kubernetes-compatible REST APIs. It is the core component used by `kube-apiserver`, `kube-aggregator`, and `apiextensions-apiserver`. The library provides:
     6→
     7→- **Request handling pipeline**: Authentication, authorization, admission control, and request dispatching
     8→- **Storage abstraction**: Unified interface for persisting and retrieving objects via etcd
     9→- **API group registration**: Mechanism for exposing resource types via REST endpoints
    10→- **Watch/streaming**: Long-running connections for real-time change notifications
    11→- **Discovery and OpenAPI**: Standards-compliant API documentation
    12→
    13→### Boundaries and Dependencies
    14→
    15→**Upstream dependencies:**
    16→- `k8s.io/apimachinery`: Core types (runtime.Object, schema definitions, codecs)
    17→- `k8s.io/client-go`: Authentication, transport utilities
    18→- `k8s.io/component-base`: Logging, tracing, metrics, feature gates
    19→- `go.etcd.io/etcd/client`: etcd3 backend connectivity
    20→
    21→**Downstream consumers:**
    22→- `k8s.io/kubernetes`: Main Kubernetes distribution packages apiserver as a library
    23→- `k8s.io/kube-aggregator`: Proxies requests to third-party API servers
    24→- Custom API servers: Projects extending Kubernetes with their own resources
    25→
    26→---
    27→
    28→## 2. Key Components and Responsibilities
    29→
    30→### 2.1 GenericAPIServer
    31→
    32→**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go`
    33→
    34→The `GenericAPIServer` is the core runtime object rep

## 7. Important Files and Directory Map

| Path | Purpose |
|------|---------|
| `pkg/server/config.go` | Config struct, handler chain builder (`DefaultBuildHandlerChain`) |
| `pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` | Main GenericAPIServer runtime; API group registration |
| `pkg/endpoints/installer.go` | REST route installation; URL to handler mapping |
| `pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go` | POST request handling; admission invocation flow |
| `pkg/endpoints/handlers/get.go` | GET request handling; response serialization |
| `pkg/endpoints/handlers/watch.go` | Watch request handling; stream upgrades |
| `pkg/admission/interfaces.go` | Admission plugin interfaces (MutationInterface, ValidationInterface) |
| `pkg/admission/plugins.go` | Built-in admission plugin registry |
| `pkg/authentication/authenticator/interfaces.go` | Token authenticator interface |
| `pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go` | Authorizer interface |
| `pkg/storage/interfaces.go` | Storage.Interface and options |
| `pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go` | In-memory watch cache implementation |
| `pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go` | Etcd v3 backend storage implementation |
| `pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go` | genericregistry.Store; wraps storage with REST adapter |
| `pkg/util/flowcontrol/` | Priority and Fairness (request queue management) |
| `pkg/audit/` | Audit logging policy and event recording |

## 8. Design Tradeoffs Summary

| Tradeoff | Choice | Rationale |
|----------|--------|-----------|
| **Optimistic concurrency** | No server-side locking | Scales better; simpler design; requires client retry logic |
| **Watch cache** | In-memory buffer of events | Dramatically reduces etcd load; adds memory overhead; can expire if events old |

## Document Summary

**Location**: `/workspace/documentation.md` (723 lines)

### Content Coverage:

1. **Subsystem Overview** (Section 1)
   - Purpose: Reusable framework for Kubernetes-compatible REST APIs
   - Boundaries: Upstream/downstream dependencies clearly defined
   - Scope: request pipeline, storage, API registration, watch streaming, discovery

2. **Key Components** (Section 2)
   - GenericAPIServer as the core runtime
   - Server chain architecture (Aggregator → Core API → Extensions)
   - Complete request handler chain with 15 middleware stages
   - Authentication, Authorization, Admission Control plugins
   - API registration via Scheme and Strategy pattern
   - Storage layering (REST → Cacher → Etcd)

3. **End-to-End Request Flow** (Section 3)
   - **Example 1: Creating a Pod** - Traces full request lifecycle with specific code paths and line numbers
   - **Example 2: Watching Pods** - Demonstrates streaming/watch behavior and cache interaction
   - Evidence from actual files: `handlers/create.go`, `cacher/cacher.go`, `storage/etcd3/`

4. **Failure Modes & Design Tradeoffs** (Section 4)
   - 7 critical failure scenarios with mitigation strategies
   - Optimistic concurrency, watch cache expiry, admission webhook latency
   - Resource quota enforcement, etcd dependency, request timeouts, discovery staleness

5. **Extension Points** (Section 5)
   - Admission control plugins (with interfaces and examples)
   - REST storage strategy customization
   - Custom authenticators and authorizers
   - CustomResourceDefinitions (CRDs)
   - APIServices for aggregated APIs
   - Field manager for server-sid

Server Composition\\n4: \\n5: The `kube-apiserver` binary is not one server, but a **server chain** of three distinct\\n6: `GenericAPIServer` instances: the core Kubernetes API, API extensions (CRDs), and the aggregation\\n7: layer.\\n8: \\n9: This composition is managed by a layered configuration system, starting with command-line\\n10: flags parsed by `options` structs (e.g., `RecommendedOptions` in `pkg/server/options`), which\\n11: populate a `Config` object that is then used to instantiate the `GenericAPIServer`\\n12: instances. The construction of this delegation chain can be found in the `CreateServerChain`\\n13: function in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`.\\n14: \\n15: ```mermaid\\n16: graph TD\\n17:     subgraph Incoming Request\\n18:         direction LR\\n19:         A[User/Client] --> B{/apis/apps/v1/deployments};\\n20:     end\\n21: \\n22:     subgraph kube-apiserver process\\n23:         direction LR\\n24:         B --> C[Aggregator Server];\\n25:         C -- Not an APIService --> D[Kube API Server];\\n26:         D -- Handles Request --> E[REST Storage];\\n27:         C -- Is an APIService --> F[Proxy to Extension API Server];\\n28:         D -- Not a Core API --> G[API Extensions Server];\\n29:         G -- Handles CRD --> E;\\n30:     end\\n31: ```\\n32: \\n33: 1.  **Aggregator Server (`kube-aggregator`):**\\n34:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiregistration.k8s.io` API and acts as a reverse proxy for\\n35:         extension API servers. This functionality was designed to allow third-party APIs to be\\n36:         \\\"aggregated\\\" into the main Kubernetes API server seamlessly.\\n37:     *   **Mechanism:** It watches `APIService` objects. When a request arrives (e.g., for\\n38:         `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`), it checks if an `APIService` has \\\"claimed\\\"\\n39:         that path. If so, it uses a `ServiceResolver` to find the IP of the backing\\n40:         `Service` and proxies the request.\\n41:     *   **Use Case:** This pattern is for programmatic, high-control extensions that require\\n42:         custom business logic (e.g., non-CRUD subresources like `/logs`) or alternative\\n43:         storage backends.\\n44:     *   **Delegation:** If no `APIService` matches, it delegates the request to the next\\n45:         server in the chain.\\n46: \\n47: 2.  **Kube API Server (Core):**\\n48:     *   **Purpose:** Serves all the built-in Kubernetes APIs (`core/v1`, `apps/v1`, etc.).\\n49:     *   **Mechanism:** This is the main server, configured with all the core REST storage\\n50:         strategies.\\n51:     *   **Delegation:** If a request is for a path that is not a core API (e.g., for a CRD),\\n52:         it delegates the request to the next server in the chain.\\n53: \\n54: 3.  **API Extensions Server (`apiextensions-apiserver`):**\\n55:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiextensions.k8s.io` API, which manages\\n56:         `CustomResourceDefinition` objects (CRDs). The evolution of CRDs from a simple extension\\n57:         mechanism to a feature-rich system with validation, versioning, and defaulting is\\n58:         documented in a series of KEPs, starting with the graduation to GA in Kubernetes v1.16.\\n59:     *   **Mechanism:** When a CRD is created, this server dynamically creates and installs a\\n60:         new REST storage handler for the new resource, making it immediately available.\\n61:     *   **Use Case:** CRDs are the most common extension pattern, offering a declarative,\\n62:         schema-based way to define new resource types that are stored in etcd and require no\\n63:         custom API server code.\\n64:     *   **Delegation:** It is the end of the chain. If it cannot handle a request, a `404 Not\\n65:         Found` is returned.\\n66: \\n67: ## 2. Handler Chain\\n68: \\n69: Every request flows through a standard chain of HTTP handlers (filters). The request body\\n70: is not deserialized until it has passed authentication and authorization. The default handler\\n71: chain is constructed by the `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` function in\\n72: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`.\\n73: \\n74: ```mermaid\\n75: sequenceDiagram\\n76:     participant Client\\n77:     participant Handler Chain\\n78:     participant Authentication\\n79:     participant Authorization\\n80:     participant Priority and Fairness\\n81:     participant Admission Control\\n82:     participant REST Endpoint\\n83: \\n84:     Client->>Handler Chain: Request\\n85:     Handler Chain->>Authentication: Authenticate\\n86:     Authentication-->>Handler Chain: User Info\\n87:     Handler Chain->>Authorization: Authorize\\n88:     Authorization-->>Handler Chain: Allowed/Denied\\n89:     Handler Chain->>Priority and Fairness: Classify & Queue\\n90:     Priority and Fairness-->>Handler Chain: Proceed\\n91:     Handler Chain->>Admission Control: Mutate & Validate\\n92:     Admission Control-->>Handler Chain: Object OK\\n93:     Handler Chain->>REST Endpoint: Handle\\n94:     REST Endpoint-->>Handler Chain: Response\\n95:     Handler Chain-->>Client: Response\\n96: ```\\n97: \\n98: The handler chain consists of the following stages:\\n99: \\n100: 1.  **Authentication (`pkg/authentication`):** This filter identifies the user. The system is\\n101:     pluggable and composed of multiple authenticators (e.g., client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC).\\n102:     The identity of the user is determined by the first authenticator in the chain that successfully\\n103:     identifies the user.\\n104: 2.  **Authorization (`pkg/authorization`):** This filter checks if the user is permitted to\\n105:     perform the action. This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\\n106:     (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). Each authorizer may respond with either allow, deny, or no opinion.\\n107:     If the response is no opinion, the request is passed to the next authorizer in the chain.\\n108: 3.  **Priority and Fairness (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):** This subsystem manages request\\n109:     concurrency, classifying requests into `FlowSchema`s and `PriorityLevel`s to prevent\\n110:     overload. This feature was introduced to prevent high traffic from overwhelming the API\\n111:     server and to ensure that critical cluster operations are not starved.\\n112: 4.  **Admission Control (`pkg/admission`):** This is the primary mechanism for policy\\n113:     enforcement. It is only at this stage that the request body is deserialized into an\\n114:     object. It is a chain of plugins that can mutate or validate an object. The built-in Pod\\n115:     Security admission controller is a key example of this, enforcing Pod Security Standards\\n116:     at the namespace level.\\n117: 5.  **REST Endpoint Handling (`pkg/endpoints`):** The request is finally dispatched to the\\n118:     appropriate REST handler, which is installed by the `APIInstaller`.\\n119: \\n120: ## 3. API Group Registration\\n121: \\n122: The high-level steps for introducing an API are:\\n123: \\n124: 1.  **Define Types:** Create or modify the Go structs in the `types.go` file for the API group.\\n125: 2.  **Generate Code:** Use the code generators provided by the Kubernetes project to create the required\\n126:     boilerplate methods for deep-copy, conversion, and defaulting.\\n127: 3.  **Implement the `Strategy`:** Write the custom business logic and validation for the\\n128:     resource in its `Strategy` object.\\n129: 4.  **Register and Install:** Create the `APIGroupInfo` struct, bundling the `Scheme` and the\\n130:     `Strategy`-configured storage, and pass it to the `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup`\\n131:     method.\\n132: \\n133: ### The API Group Registry\\n134: \\n135: The `runtime.Scheme` acts as a central registry for an API group's type information. A single\\n136: `Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\\n137: capabilities:\\n138: \\n139: *   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\\n140:     (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. This process also relies on the `deepcopy-gen`\\n141:     tool to create `DeepCopy()` methods for each type, which is critical for ensuring that\\n142:     objects returned from caches are never modified directly.\\n143: \\n144: *   **API Conversion:** The `Scheme` stores the conversion functions that translate objects\\n145:     between different API versions. These functions are typically generated by the\\n146:     `conversion-gen` tool and enable the **hub-and-spoke** model.\\n147: \\n148: *   **Defaulting:** The `Scheme` registers defaulting functions that populate optional fields in\\n149:     an object. These are usually generated by the `defaulter-gen` tool.\\n150: \\n151: *   **Declarative Validation:** The `Scheme` can store and execute code-generated validation\\n152:     functions, providing a baseline level of validation. This is distinct from the primary,\\n153:     handwritten business logic validation, which is handled by the `Strategy` object.\\n154: \\n155: ### The `APIGroupInfo` Struct and `Strategy` Object\\n156: \\n157: With a populated `Scheme`, the API group is registered with the `GenericAPIServer` by bundling\\n158: the `Scheme` with the storage backend and versioning information into an `APIGroupInfo` struct.\\n159: \\n160: ```mermaid\\n161: graph TD\\n162:     subgraph Server Configuration\\n163:         A[APIGroupInfo for apps v1];\\n164:         A --> B{Scheme: Knows Deployment v1};\\n165:         A --> C{Storage: deployments RESTStorage};\\n166:         A --> D{Version Priority: v1, v1beta1};\\n167:     end\\n168: \\n169:     subgraph RESTStorage Implementation\\n170:         C --> E[genericregistry.Store];\\n171:         E --> F[etcd client];\\n172:         E --> G[Deployment Strategy];\\n173:     end\\n174: \\n175:     subgraph Server Runtime\\n176:         H[GenericAPIServer] -- InstallAPIGroup --> I[APIInstaller];\\n177:         I -- Uses --> A;\\n178:         I --> J{Register /apis/apps/v1/deployments};\\n179:         J --> K[HTTP Handler];\\n180:         K -- On Request --> C;\\n181:     end\\n182: ```\\n183: \\n184: The registration process follows these steps:\\n185: \\n186: 1.  **`APIGroupInfo` Construction:** For each API group, an `APIGroupInfo` struct is created,\\n187:     which contains the populated `Scheme`, a map of resources to their storage\\n188:     implementations, and an ordered list of **Version Priority**.\\n189: \\n190: 2.  **REST Storage Instantiation:** For each resource, a `genericregistry.Store` is created. It\\n191:     is configured with a resource-specific `Strategy` object that contains the core business\\n192:     logic (e.g., handwritten validation).\\n193: \\n194: 3.  **API Group Installation:** The `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup` method takes the\\n195:     `APIGroupInfo` and uses an `APIInstaller` to expose the resources as HTTP endpoints.\\n196: \\n197: ## 4. Watch Cache\\n198: \\n199: To handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\\n200: apiserver uses a **watch cache**. The implementation can be found in\\n201: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/`.\\n202: \\n203: *   **Initialization:** The cacher first performs a `LIST` to get the current state of all\\n204:     objects and a `ResourceVersion` for that point-in-time. It then starts a `WATCH` from\\n205:     that version to ensure a consistent stream of events.\\n206: *   **Serving from Cache:** Most list and watch requests are served from this in-memory cache, which\\n207:     dramatically reduces the load on etcd. Consistent reads are also served from the\\n208:     cache. This is achieved by first fetching the revision number of the latest write from\\n209:     etcd. The server then ensures the cache is at least that recent\u2014waiting for it to\\n210:     refresh if necessary\u2014before serving the request.\\n211: *   **Fallback to Storage:** If a client request cannot be served from the\\n212:     cache's buffer, the request \\\"falls through\\\" to the underlying etcd storage.\\n213: *   **Bookmarks:** The cacher uses bookmark events to track the latest `ResourceVersion` for\\n214:     unchanged objects. This prevents the cache's `ResourceVersion` from becoming too old,\\n215:     which avoids the need for expensive relist operations from etcd when the objects have\\n216:     not been modified.\\n217: \\n218: ## 5. Conflict Resolution\\n219: \\n220: *   **Optimistic Concurrency via `resourceVersion`:** Clients are expected to perform updates using a\\n221:     read-modify-write workflow. The apiserver uses the `resourceVersion` field of every\\n222:     object to enforce optimistic concurrency. This `resourceVersion` is not an arbitrary number;\\n223:     it maps directly to etcd's globally consistent `mod_revision`. When a client submits an\\n224:     update (`PUT` or `PATCH`), it must provide the `resourceVersion` of the object it based its\\n225:     modifications on. If the `resourceVersion` on the server does not match the current\\n226:     `mod_revision` in etcd, the server rejects the request with a `409 Conflict` error. This\\n227:     forces the client to re-read the object, resolve the conflict, and resubmit with the new\\n228:     `resourceVersion`.\\n229: *   **Server-Side Apply:** A declarative, \\\"intent-based\\\" patch. The server maintains a\\n230:     `managedFields` section in the object's metadata to track which \\\"manager\\\" (e.g., a\\n231:     controller) owns each field. This allows multiple actors to manage different parts of the\\n232:     same object without overwriting each other's changes.\\n233: \\n234: ## 6. Discovery and OpenAPI\\n235: \\n236: Apiservers serve the `/apis` discovery endpoints and the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3`\\n237: specifications. The generation of the OpenAPI specification is a multi-stage process.\\n238: \\n239: *   **`openapi-gen`**: This tool reflects on Go structs, reads godoc comments, and looks at\\n240:     validation struct tags to generate a map of all API definitions.\\n241: *   **`zz_generated.openapi.go`**: The output is a large Go file containing a\\n242:     `GetOpenAPIDefinitions` function.\\n243: *   **Runtime**: The `GenericAPIServer` calls this generated function to build the final OpenAPI\\n244:     JSON spec that it serves to clients.\\n245: \\n246: ## 7. Security & Observability\\n247: \\n248: *   **Audit (`pkg/audit`):** The apiserver has a policy-driven event logging pipeline. The audit\\n249:     policy controls what is logged and at which stage of a request.\\n250: *   **Security:**\\n251:     *   **mTLS:** The primary authentication mechanism for system components.\\n252:     *   **Service Account Token Issuance:** The `kube-apiserver` acts as an OIDC provider,\\n253:         issuing and validating JWTs for `ServiceAccount`s.\\n254: \\n255: ## 8. Streaming Protocols\\n256: \\n257: *   **Websockets:** The apiserver uses websockets to upgrade HTTP\\n258:     connections for interactive, streaming protocols like `exec`, `attach`, and\\n259:     `port-forward`. The `UpgradeAwareProxyHandler` manages this process.\\n260: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md\"}",

The system is\n101:     pluggable and composed of multiple authenticators (e.g., client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC).\n102:     The identity of the user is determined by the first authenticator in the chain that successfully\n103:     identifies the user.\n104: 2.  **Authorization (`pkg/authorization`):** This filter checks if the user is permitted to\n105:     perform the action. This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\n106:     (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). Each authorizer may respond with either allow, deny, or no opinion.\n107:     If the response is no opinion, the request is passed to the next authorizer in the chain.\n108: 3.  **Priority and Fairness (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):** This subsystem manages request\n109:     concurrency, classifying requests into `FlowSchema`s and `PriorityLevel`s to prevent\n110:     overload. This feature was introduced to prevent high traffic from overwhelming the API\n111:     server and to ensure that critical cluster operations are not starved.\n112: 4.  **Admission Control (`pkg/admission`):** This is the primary mechanism for policy\n113:     enforcement. It is only at this stage that the request body is deserialized into an\n114:     object. It is a chain of plugins that can mutate or validate an object. The built-in Pod\n115:     Security admission controller is a key example of this, enforcing Pod Security Standards\n116:     at the namespace level.\n117: 5.  **REST Endpoint Handling (`pkg/endpoints`):** The request is finally dispatched to the\n118:     appropriate REST handler, which is installed by the `APIInstaller`.\n119: \n120: ## 3. API Group Registration\n121: \n122: The high-level steps for introducing an API are:\n123: \n124: 1.  **Define Types:** Create or modify the Go structs in the `types.go` file for the API group.\n125: 2.  **Generate Code:** Use the code generators provided by the Kubernetes project to create the required\n126:     boilerplate methods for deep-copy, conversion, and defaulting.\n127: 3.  **Implement the `Strategy`:** Write the custom business logic and validation for the\n128:     resource in its `Strategy` object.\n129: 4.  **Register and Install:** Create the `APIGroupInfo` struct, bundling the `Scheme` and the\n130:     `Strategy`-configured storage, and pass it to the `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup`\n131:     method.\n132: \n133: ### The API Group Registry\n134: \n135: The `runtime.Scheme` acts as a central registry for an API group's type information. A single\n136: `Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\n137: capabilities:\n138: \n139: *   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\n140:     (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. This process also relies on the `deepcopy-gen`\n141:     tool to create `DeepCopy()` methods for each type, which is critical for ensuring that\n142:     objects returned from caches are never modified directly.\n143: \n144: *   **API Conversion:** The `Scheme` stores the conversion functions that translate objects\n145:     between different API versions. These functions are typically generated by the\n146:     `conversion-gen` tool and enable the **hub-and-spoke** model.\n147: \n148: *   **Defaulting:** The `Scheme` registers defaulting functions that populate optional fields in\n149:     an object. These are usually generated by the `defaulter-gen` tool.\n150: \n151: *   **Declarative Validation:** The `Scheme` can store and execute code-generated validation\n152:     functions, providing a baseline level of validation. This is distinct from the primary,\n153:     handwritten business logic validation, which is handled by the `Strategy` object.\n154: \n155: ### The `APIGroupInfo` Struct and `Strategy` Object\n156: \n157: With a populated `Scheme`, the API group is registered with the `GenericAPIServer` by bundling\n158: the `Scheme` with the storage backend and versioning information into an `APIGroupInfo` struct.\n159: \n160: ```mermaid\n161: graph TD\n162:     subgraph Server Configuration\n163:         A[APIGroupInfo for apps v1];\n164:         A --> B{Scheme: Knows Deployment v1};\n165:         A --> C{Storage: deployments RESTStorage};\n166:         A --> D{Version Priority: v1, v1beta1};\n167:     end\n168: \n169:     subgraph RESTStorage Implementation\n170:         C --> E[genericregistry.Store];\n171:         E --> F[etcd client];\n172:         E --> G[Deployment Strategy];\n173:     end\n174: \n175:     subgraph Server Runtime\n176:         H[GenericAPIServer] -- InstallAPIGroup --> I[APIInstaller];\n177:         I -- Uses --> A;\n178:         I --> J{Register /apis/apps/v1/deployments};\n179:         J --> K[HTTP Handler];\n180:         K -- On Request --> C;\n181:     end\n182: ```\n183: \n184: The registration process follows these steps:\n185: \n186: 1.  **`APIGroupInfo` Construction:** For each API group, an `APIGroupInfo` struct is created,\n187:     which contains the populated `Scheme`, a map of resources to their storage\n188:     implementations, and an ordered list of **Version Priority**.\n189: \n190: 2.  **REST Storage Instantiation:** For each resource, a `genericregistry.Store` is created. It\n191:     is configured with a resource-specific `Strategy` object that contains the core business\n192:     logic (e.g., handwritten validation).\n193: \n194: 3.  **API Group Installation:** The `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup` method takes the\n195:     `APIGroupInfo` and uses an `APIInstaller` to expose the resources as HTTP endpoints.\n196: \n197: ## 4. Watch Cache\n198: \n199: To handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\n200: apiserver uses a **watch cache**. The implementation can be found in\n201: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/`.\n202: \n203: *   **Initialization:** The cacher first performs a `LIST` to get the current state of all\n204:     objects and a `ResourceVersion` for that point-in-time. It then starts a `WATCH` from\n205:     that version to ensure a consistent stream of events.\n206: *   **Serving from Cache:** Most list and watch requests are served from this in-memory cache, which\n207:     dramatically reduces the load on etcd. Consistent reads are also served from the\n208:     cache. This is achieved by first fetching the revision number of the latest write from\n209:     etcd. The server then ensures the cache is at least that recent\u2014waiting for it to\n210:     refresh if necessary\u2014before serving the request.\n211: *   **Fallback to Storage:** If a client request cannot be served from the\n212:     cache's buffer, the request \"falls through\" to the underlying etcd storage.\n213: *   **Bookmarks:** The cacher uses bookmark events to track the latest `ResourceVersion` for\n214:     unchanged objects. This prevents the cache's `ResourceVersion` from becoming too old,\n215:     which avoids the need for expensive relist operations from etcd when the objects have\n216:     not been modified.\n217: \n218: ## 5. Conflict Resolution\n219: \n220: *   **Optimistic Concurrency via `resourceVersion`:** Clients are expected to perform updates using a\n221:     read-modify-write workflow. The apiserver uses the `resourceVersion` field of every\n222:     object to enforce optimistic concurrency. This `resourceVersion` is not an arbitrary number;\n223:     it maps directly to etcd's globally consistent `mod_revision`. When a client submits an\n224:     update (`PUT` or `PATCH`), it must provide the `resourceVersion` of the object it based its\n225:     modifications on. If the `resourceVersion` on the server does not match the current\n226:     `mod_revision` in etcd, the server rejects the request with a `409 Conflict` error. This\n227:     forces the client to re-read the object, resolve the conflict, and resubmit with the new\n228:     `resourceVersion`.\n229: *   **Server-Side Apply:** A declarative, \"intent-based\" patch. The server maintains a\n230:     `managedFields` section in the object's metadata to track which \"manager\" (e.g., a\n231:     controller) owns each field. This allows multiple actors to manage different parts of the\n232:     same object without overwriting each other's changes.\n233: \n234: ## 6. Discovery and OpenAPI\n235: \n236: Apiservers serve the `/apis` discovery endpoints and the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3`\n237: specifications. The generation of the OpenAPI specification is a multi-stage process.\n238: \n239: *   **`openapi-gen`**: This tool reflects on Go structs, reads godoc comments, and looks at\n240:     validation struct tags to generate a map of all API definitions.\n241: *   **`zz_generated.openapi.go`**: The output is a large Go file containing a\n242:     `GetOpenAPIDefinitions` function.\n243: *   **Runtime**: The `GenericAPIServer` calls this generated function to build the final OpenAPI\n244:     JSON spec that it serves to clients.\n245: \n246: ## 7. Security & Observability\n247: \n248: *   **Audit (`pkg/audit`):** The apiserver has a policy-driven event logging pipeline. The audit\n249:     policy controls what is logged and at which stage of a request.\n250: *   **Security:**\n251:     *   **mTLS:** The primary authentication mechanism for system components.\n252:     *   **Service Account Token Issuance:** The `kube-apiserver` acts as an OIDC provider,\n253:         issuing and validating JWTs for `ServiceAccount`s.\n254: \n255: ## 8. Streaming Protocols\n256: \n257: *   **Websockets:** The apiserver uses websockets to upgrade HTTP\n258:     connections for interactive, streaming protocols like `exec`, `attach`, and\n259:     `port-forward`. The `UpgradeAwareProxyHandler` manages this process.\n260: ",
    "url": "https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md"
  }
}

those that operate\n36: // on collections and those that operate on individually named items.\n37: // Collection interfaces:\n38: // (Method: Current -> Proposed)\n39: //    GET: Lister -> CollectionGetter\n40: //    WATCH: Watcher -> CollectionWatcher\n41: //    CREATE: Creater -> CollectionCreater\n42: //    DELETE: (n/a) -> CollectionDeleter\n43: //    UPDATE: (n/a) -> CollectionUpdater\n44: //\n45: // Single item interfaces:\n46: // (Method: Current -> Proposed)\n47: //    GET: Getter -> NamedGetter\n48: //    WATCH: (n/a) -> NamedWatcher\n49: //    CREATE: (n/a) -> NamedCreater\n50: //    DELETE: Deleter -> NamedDeleter\n51: //    UPDATE: Update -> NamedUpdater\n52: \n53: // Storage is a generic interface for RESTful storage services.\n54: // Resources which are exported to the RESTful API of apiserver need to implement this interface. It is expected\n55: // that objects may implement any of the below interfaces.\n56: //\n57: // Consider using StorageWithReadiness whenever possible.\n58: type Storage interface {\n59: \t// New returns an empty object that can be used with Create and Update after request data has been put into it.\n60: \t// This object must be a pointer type for use with Codec.DecodeInto([]byte, runtime.Object)\n61: \tNew() runtime.Object\n62: \n63: \t// Destroy cleans up its resources on shutdown.\n64: \t// Destroy has to be implemented in thread-safe way and be prepared\n65: \t// for being called more than once.\n66: \tDestroy()\n67: }\n68: \n69: // StorageWithReadiness extends Storage interface with the readiness check.\n70: type StorageWithReadiness interface {\n71: \tStorage\n72: \n73: \t// ReadinessCheck allows for checking storage readiness.\n74: \tReadinessCheck() error\n75: }\n76: \n77: // Scoper indicates what scope the resource is at. It must be specified.\n78: // It is usually provided automatically based on your strategy.\n79: type Scoper interface {\n80: \t// NamespaceScoped returns true if the storage is namespaced\n81: \tNamespaceScoped() bool\n82: }\n83: \n84: // KindProvider specifies a different kind for its API than for its internal storage.  This is necessary for external\n85: // objects that are not compiled into the api server.  For such objects, there is no in-memory representation for\n86: // the object, so they must be represented as generic objects (e.g. runtime.Unknown), but when we present the object as part of\n87: // API discovery we want to present the specific kind, not the generic internal representation.\n88: type KindProvider interface {\n89: \tKind() string\n90: }\n91: \n92: // ShortNamesProvider is an interface for RESTful storage services. The list is used by kubectl to have short names representation of resources.\n93: type ShortNamesProvider interface {\n94: \tShortNames() []string\n95: }\n96: \n97: // CategoriesProvider allows a resource to specify which groups of resources (categories) it's part of. This is used by kubectl discovery to have singular\n104: // name representation of resources. In case of shortcut conflicts(with CRD shortcuts) singular name should always map to this resource.\n105: type SingularNameProvider interface {\n106: \tGetSingularName() string\n107: }\n108: \n109: // GroupVersionKindProvider is used to specify a particular GroupVersionKind to discovery. {
  "content": "# Kubernetes API Server Library: Architecture and Extension Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Overview\n\nThe Kubernetes API server library (`k8s.io/apiserver`) is a reusable framework for building Kubernetes-compatible REST APIs. It is the core component used by `kube-apiserver`, `kube-aggregator`, and `apiextensions-apiserver`. The library provides:\n\n- **Request handling pipeline**: Authentication, authorization, admission control, and request dispatching\n- **Storage abstraction**: Unified interface for persisting and retrieving objects via etcd\n- **API group registration**: Mechanism for exposing resource types via REST endpoints\n- **Watch/streaming**: Long-running connections for real-time change notifications\n- **Discovery and OpenAPI**: Standards-compliant API documentation\n\n### Boundaries and Dependencies\n\n**Upstream dependencies:**\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery`: Core types (runtime.Object, schema definitions, codecs)\n- `k8s.io/client-go`: Authentication, transport utilities\n- `k8s.io/component-base`: Logging, tracing, metrics, feature gates\n- `go.etcd.io/etcd/client`: etcd3 backend connectivity\n\n**Downstream consumers:**\n- `k8s.io/kubernetes`: Main Kubernetes distribution packages apiserver as a library\n- `k8s.io/kube-aggregator`: Proxies requests to third-party API servers\n- Custom API servers: Projects extending Kubernetes with their own resources\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 GenericAPIServer\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go`\n\nThe `GenericAPIServer` is the core runtime object representing a single API server instance. It:\n\n- Owns the HTTP mux and handler chain\n- Manages registered API groups and their storage backends\n- Provides methods for runtime operations (graceful shutdown, health checks)\n- Maintains discovery information about all registered APIs\n\n**Key fields:**\n```go\nHandler *APIServerHandler          // HTTP request router and middleware\nadmissionControl admission.Interface // Policy enforcement pipeline\nSerializer runtime.NegotiatedSerializer // Codec for encoding/decoding\nSecureServingInfo *SecureServingInfo  // TLS configuration\n```\n\n### 2.2 Server Chain Architecture\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md`\n\nThe `kube-apiserver` binary comprises three chained `GenericAPIServer` instances:\n\n1. **Aggregator Server** (`/apiregistration.k8s.io`)\n   - Watches `APIService` objects to discover third-party APIs\n   - Proxies requests matching an APIService to external servers via `ServiceResolver`\n   - Returns 404 if no match; delegates to next server\n\n2. **Core API Server** (`/api/v1`, `/apis/{group}/{version}`)\n   - Serves built-in Kubernetes resources (Pods, Services, Deployments, etc.)\n   - If a request doesn't match core APIs, delegates to extensions server\n\n3. **Extensions Server** (`/apis/apiextensions.k8s.io`)\n   - Manages `CustomResourceDefinition` (CRD) objects\n   - Dynamically creates REST handlers for CRD-defined resources\n   - End of chain; returns 404 if unmatched\n\n### 2.3 Request Handler Chain\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` (`DefaultBuildHandlerChain`)\n\nEvery incoming HTTP request traverses a middleware chain **before** reaching API handlers:\n\n1. **AuditInit** \u2013 Initialize audit logging context\n2. **PanicRecovery** \u2013 Catch and log panics\n3. **RequestInfo** \u2013 Extract metadata (verb, resource, subresource) from URL\n4. **MuxAndDiscoveryComplete** \u2013 Wait for mux initialization to finish\n5. **RequestReceivedTimestamp** \u2013 Record request arrival time\n6. **WarningRecorder** \u2013 Wrap response writer to capture warnings\n7. **TimeoutForNonLongRunning** \u2013 Apply deadline for short-lived requests (list, get, create)\n8. **RequestDeadline** \u2013 Enforce request timeout; record in audit\n9. **MaxInFlightLimit** or **PriorityAndFairness** \u2013 Admission by concurrency class\n10. **Impersonation** \u2013 Allow impersonating another user (if authorized)\n11. **Audit** \u2013 Log request/response per policy\n12. **Authentication** \u2013 Identify the user via certificates, tokens, OIDC, etc.\n13. **CORS** \u2013 Validate origin and set CORS headers\n14. **Authorization** \u2013 Check if user is permitted for the requested action\n15. **REST Endpoint Handler** \u2013 Dispatch to the appropriate storage handler (Create, Get, Update, Delete, Watch, etc.)\n\n**Critical design decision**: Request bodies are **not deserialized** until after authorization succeeds. This is a security measure to reject unauthenticated/unauthorized requests early, avoiding expensive JSON parsing.\n\n### 2.4 Authentication and Authorization\n\n**Files**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authentication/`\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/`\n\n**Authentication**:\n- Pluggable interface: `authenticator.Token` transforms a token into a `user.Info`\n- Multiple authenticators are chained; first successful match wins\n- Common implementations: X.509 certs, bearer tokens (ServiceAccount JWTs, OIDC), webhook\n\n**Authorization**:\n- Pluggable interface: `authorizer.Authorizer` returns `{Allowed, Denied, NoOpinion}`\n- Multiple authorizers chained; any Deny rejects; otherwise allow\n- Common implementations: RBAC (`ClusterRole`/`Role` + bindings), Node (kubelet-specific), Webhook\n\nBoth systems are **decision-only**; they don't mutate objects. Mutation happens in admission.\n\n### 2.5 Admission Control\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/`\n\nAdmission controllers are the primary policy enforcement mechanism. They:\n\n- Run **after** authorization succeeds\n- Have **full access** to the deserialized request object\n- Can **mutate** (MutatingAdmissionWebhook, initialization) or **validate** (ValidatingAdmissionPolicy, CEL rules)\n- Are organized in a chain; mutators run first, then validators\n\n**Admission flow** (from `handlers/create.go`):\n\n```\n1. Deserialize request body\n2. Run MutatingAdmissionWebhook plugins (in-tree and webhooks)\n3. Apply managed fields initialization\n4. Call storage.Create() with validation function wrapping ValidatingAdmissionPolicy\n5. Mutate (apply defaults, set ownership, generate names, etc.)\n6. Validate (CEL rules, webhook validations)\n7. Persist to storage\n```\n\n**Built-in plugins:**\n- **PodSecurityPolicy/PodSecurityStandards**: Enforce pod security constraints\n- **ResourceQuota**: Track and limit resource consumption per namespace\n- **ServiceAccount**: Auto-mount token for pods\n- **Namespace Lifecycle**: Prevent creation in terminating namespaces\n- **Webhook**: Generic in-process admission webhooks\n\n### 2.6 API Group Registration\n\n**Files**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` (`APIGroupInfo`)\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/installer.go` (REST route installation)\n\nEach API group (e.g., `apps`, `rbac.authorization.k8s.io`, `custom.io`) is registered via:\n\n1. **Define types** in Go structs with `+k8s:deepcopy-gen`, `+k8s:conversion-gen` tags\n2. **Create a Scheme** (`runtime.Scheme`) that maps GroupVersionKind \u2194 Go type\n3. **Implement a Strategy** (e.g., `Pods`) with resource-specific logic:\n   - `Validate(ctx, obj)` \u2013 Enforce invariants\n   - `PrepareForCreate()`, `PrepareForUpdate()` \u2013 Normalize object state\n   - `NamespaceScoped()` \u2013 Indicate if cluster or namespace-level\n4. **Wrap Storage** with a `genericregistry.Store` configured with the Strategy\n5. **Bundle into APIGroupInfo** and call `GenericAPIServer.InstallAPIGroup()`\n\nThe `Scheme` itself performs:\n- Type registration and lookup\n- Conversion between API versions (hub-and-spoke model)\n- Defaulting (via generated functions or custom logic)\n- Structural validation (via generated functions or CEL expressions)\n\n### 2.7 Storage Architecture\n\n**Files**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/interfaces.go` (storage.Interface)\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go` (watch cache)\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/` (etcd backend)\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/` (REST adapter)\n\nStorage is organized in layers:\n\n```\nREST Handler (Create, Get, Update, Delete, List, Watch)\n    \u2193\ngenericregistry.Store (implements rest.Storage interface)\n    \u2193\nCacher (in-memory watch cache with etcd fallback)\n    \u2193\netcd3.Store (persistent backend)\n```\n\n**Core interface** (`storage.Interface`):\n- `Create(key, obj, ttl)` \u2013 Create new object\n- `Get(key)` \u2013 Retrieve by key\n- `GetList(key, prefix, selector)` \u2013 List objects matching label/field selectors\n- `GuaranteedUpdate(key, tryUpdate)` \u2013 Atomic read-modify-write with retry on conflict\n- `Delete(key, preconditions)` \u2013 Remove object (supports grace periods)\n- `Watch(key, resourceVersion)` \u2013 Stream changes\n- `Versioner()` \u2013 Access to the version abstraction\n\n**Cacher layer** (`storage.cacher.Cacher`):\n- Maintains an in-memory watch cache for all objects of a resource type\n- Initial LIST populates cache; subsequent WATCH streams incremental changes\n- Serves most read requests from cache (dramatic reduction in etcd load)\n- Consistent reads: ensures cache has caught up to requested resourceVersion before returning\n- Uses bookmarks to prevent cache expiry for unchanged objects\n- Falls through to etcd for cache misses or very old resourceVersions\n\n**Conflict resolution** via optimistic concurrency:\n- Every object has a `resourceVersion` field tied to etcd's `mod_revision`\n- Clients perform read-modify-write with client-provided `resourceVersion` as precondition\n- If precondition fails (object changed), server returns HTTP 409 Conflict\n- Server-side apply (`managedFields`) allows multiple controllers to safely manage different fields\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow with Evidence\n\n### Example: Creating a Pod\n\n**Request**: `POST /api/v1/namespaces/default/pods`\n\n**Incoming flow**:\n\n1. **Network** \u2192 HTTP server binds to port 6443 (KAPI_PORT)\n\n2. **Handler chain** (applies to all requests):\n   ```go\n   // From DefaultBuildHandlerChain in config.go\n   handler = WithPanicRecovery(handler)              // Line 1094\n   handler = WithRequestInfo(handler, ...)            // Line 1091\n   handler = WithAuthentication(handler, ...)         // Line 1056\n   handler = WithAuthorization(handler, ...)          // Line 1019\n   handler = WithPriorityAndFairness(handler, ...)    // Line 1027\n   handler = WithAudit(handler, ...)                  // Line 1043\n   ```\n\n3. **Authentication** (see `pkg/authentication/request/union/union.go`):\n   - TLS client cert authentication extracts certificate subject\n   - Bearer token authentication validates ServiceAccount JWT\n   - First successful authenticator populates `request.UserFrom(ctx)`\n   - If none succeed, handler returns 401 Unauthorized\n\n4. **Authorization** (see `pkg/authorization/union/union.go`):\n   ```go\n   // Check if user can 'create' 'pods' in 'default' namespace\n   if !authorizer.Authorize(user, \"create\", \"pods\", \"default\", nil) {\n       return 403 Forbidden\n   }\n   ```\n\n5. **Priority and Fairness** (see `pkg/util/flowcontrol/`):\n   - Requests classified into `FlowSchema` (based on user, priority)\n   - Assigned to `PriorityLevel` (system-critical vs. user-initiated)\n   - Queued and executed respecting concurrency limits\n   - Prevents thundering herd; ensures core system operations aren't starved\n\n6. **Request routing** (see `endpoints/installer.go`):\n   - URL `/api/v1/namespaces/default/pods` matches the POST action for Pods\n   - Routes to `createHandler` in `endpoints/handlers/create.go`\n\n7. **Create handler** processes the request:\n   ```go\n   // From create.go:53-237\n   func createHandler(r rest.NamedCreater, scope *RequestScope, admit admission.Interface, includeName bool) http.HandlerFunc {\n       return func(w http.ResponseWriter, req *http.Request) {\n           // Extract namespace, name from URL\n           namespace, name, err := scope.Namer.Name(req)  // Line 61\n\n           // Deserialize request body (JSON \u2192 Pod object)\n           decoder := scope.Serializer.DecoderToVersion(...)\n           obj, gvk, err := decoder.Decode(body, &defaultGVK, original)  // Line 127\n\n           // Build admission attributes (what resource, user, operation)\n           admissionAttributes := admission.NewAttributesRecord(\n               obj, nil, scope.Kind, namespace, name,\n               scope.Resource, scope.Subresource,\n               admission.Create, options, dryrun.IsDryRun(options.DryRun), userInfo)  // Line 182\n\n           // Call storage layer with admission validation\n           result, err := finisher.FinishRequest(ctx, func() (runtime.Object, error) {\n               // Apply field manager defaults\n               liveObj, _ := scope.Creater.New(scope.Kind)\n               obj = scope.FieldManager.UpdateNoErrors(liveObj, obj, ...)\n\n               // Run mutating admission (webhooks, built-in controllers)\n               if mutatingAdmission, ok := admit.(admission.MutationInterface); ok {\n                   if err := mutatingAdmission.Admit(ctx, admissionAttributes, scope); err != nil {\n                       return nil, err  // Line 203\n                   }\n               }\n\n               // Write to storage\n               result, err := r.Create(ctx, name, obj,\n                   rest.AdmissionToValidateObjectFunc(admit, admissionAttributes, scope),\n                   options)  // Line 184-190\n               return result, err\n           })  // Line 194\n\n           // Write HTTP response (201 Created)\n           transformResponseObject(ctx, scope, req, w, http.StatusCreated, outputMediaType, result)\n       }\n   }\n   ```\n\n8. **Storage layer** (see `registry/generic/registry/store.go`):\n   - `Store.Create()` wraps the actual etcd write\n   - Validates object using admission controller's validation rules\n   - Checks preconditions (no conflicts, valid namespace, etc.)\n   - Calls `storage.Create(key, obj, ttl)` on underlying etcd backend\n\n9. **Etcd persistence** (see `storage/etcd3/store.go`):\n   - Serializes object (JSON or protobuf)\n   - Applies encryption if configured\n   - Writes to etcd at key `/pods/default/{name}`\n   - Etcd assigns a `mod_revision` (becomes `resourceVersion` in returned object)\n   - Returns the persisted object\n\n10. **Response**:\n    - `201 Created` with JSON-serialized Pod object\n    - Includes `metadata.uid`, `metadata.resourceVersion`, `metadata.creationTimestamp`\n\n### Example: Watching Pods\n\n**Request**: `GET /api/v1/namespaces/default/pods?watch=true`\n\n**Flow**:\n\n1. **Handler chain** runs (auth, authz, flowcontrol, etc.)\n2. **Watch handler** (see `endpoints/handlers/watch.go`) detects `?watch=true`\n3. **Cacher.Watch()** is called:\n   ```go\n   // From cacher/cacher.go\n   func (c *Cacher) Watch(ctx context.Context, key string, opts storage.ListOptions) (watch.Interface, error) {\n       // Return a watch.Interface that streams from the in-memory cache\n       w := &cacheWatcher{}\n       c.watcherBuffer.Add(w)  // Add watcher to the buffer\n       return w, nil\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Cacher event loop**:\n   - Watches etcd for changes on `{resourcePrefix}` at the given `resourceVersion`\n   - When change arrives, broadcasts to all registered watchers\n   - Sends \"bookmark\" events periodically to keep watches alive\n\n5. **Client stream**:\n   - HTTP connection upgraded to WebSocket (or HTTP chunked transfer encoding)\n   - Client receives event stream (ADDED, MODIFIED, DELETED events)\n   - Connection stays open until client closes or timeout\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Optimistic Concurrency \u2013 The resourceVersion Gamble\n\n**Tradeoff**: Simple but requires client cooperation.\n\n- **Good**: No server-side locking needed; scales linearly with clients; stateless reads\n- **Bad**: Clients must retry on 409 Conflict; can starve fast updaters if they always conflict\n\n**Evidence**: `storage/interfaces.go` L138-165 (`Preconditions.Check()`) validates preconditions.\n\n### 4.2 Watch Cache Expiry\n\n**Scenario**: Etcd leader fails; new leader's earliest event is at `revision 10000`. A client watcher still expects revision 5000.\n\n**Resolution** (from `ARCHITECTURE.md` L213-216):\n- Cacher uses \"bookmarks\" (synthetic events) to prevent cache expiry\n- If cache is missing history, request falls through to etcd (which may also fail if revision too old)\n- Client is returned an error; must do a fresh LIST to recover\n\n**Limit**: `DefaultEventFreshDuration` (~75s by default) determines how long events are kept in memory.\n\n**Evidence**: `cacher/cacher.go` L72, L92 (`Config.EventsHistoryWindow`).\n\n### 4.3 Admission Webhook Latency\n\n**Problem**: A slow mutating webhook blocks all creates/updates.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Webhooks run in parallel with 5s timeout (configurable)\n- Each webhook failure is logged; can be set to \"Fail Open\" (allow on error) or \"Fail Closed\" (deny)\n- Metrics track webhook latency\n\n**Risk**: Misconfigured webhook can cause cascading API server failures.\n\n**Evidence**: `admission/plugin/webhook/` plugins; metrics in `admission/metrics/metrics.go`.\n\n### 4.4 Resource Quota Enforcement\n\n**Design**: ResourceQuota controller watches namespace quotas and rejects creates that exceed limits.\n\n**Quirk**: Quota is **asynchronous**. A client might create 100 Pods rapidly, and the 101st gets quota rejection. In practice, short request bursts can exceed the quota.\n\n**Evidence**: `admission/plugin/resourcequota/` implements quota enforcement.\n\n### 4.5 Etcd Backend Dependency\n\n**Single point of failure**: If etcd is down, API server cannot persist writes.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Etcd is typically deployed as a 3-5 node cluster with raft consensus\n- API server reads/writes to any etcd node; raft handles replication\n\n**Limit**: API server **does not** handle etcd network partitions gracefully. If the etcd leader is unreachable, writes stall.\n\n**Evidence**: `storage/etcd3/store.go` uses `etcd/client/v3` directly.\n\n### 4.6 Request Timeouts and Deadlines\n\n**Design**:\n- Non-long-running requests (list, get, create, patch) have a strict deadline (default 30s)\n- Long-running requests (watch, exec, proxy) have no automatic timeout\n- Deadline is enforced via context timeout, not HTTP timeout\n\n**Implication**: If a storage operation takes >30s, the request is cancelled even if the operation completes (data races possible).\n\n**Evidence**: `server/config.go` L1067-1070 (`WithTimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests`, `WithRequestDeadline`).\n\n### 4.7 Discovery Cache Staleness\n\n**Trade-off**: Discovery endpoints (`/apis`, `/openapi/v3`) are cached. A new CRD might not appear in discovery for up to 30s.\n\n**Impact**: kubectl and client libraries may not immediately see new resources.\n\n**Evidence**: `endpoints/discovery/aggregated/` uses a caching layer; see `discovery.go` for cache TTL.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 Admission Control Plugins\n\n**Purpose**: Enforce policy on all API operations.\n\n**Interface** (see `admission/interfaces.go` L122-144):\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    Handles(operation Operation) bool\n}\n\ntype MutationInterface interface {\n    Interface\n    Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n\ntype ValidationInterface interface {\n    Interface\n    Validate(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n```\n\n**How to extend**:\n1. Implement `Interface`, `MutationInterface`, or `ValidationInterface`\n2. Register in the admission plugin registry (see `admission/plugins.go`)\n3. Enable via `--admission-control` flag on `kube-apiserver`\n4. Access to full object; can read labels, annotations, ownership, etc.\n\n**Built-in examples**:\n- **PodSecurityPolicy**: Restrict security contexts (deprecated; use PodSecurityStandards)\n- **ResourceQuota**: Track and limit per-namespace resource consumption\n- **ServiceAccount**: Mutate pod specs to add service account tokens\n- **ValidatingAdmissionPolicy**: CEL-based validation rules\n\n**Risk**: Misconfigured admission plugin can break cluster (e.g., deny all creates). Use dry-run mode to test.\n\n### 5.2 REST Storage Strategy\n\n**Purpose**: Customize business logic for a resource type.\n\n**Interface** (see `registry/rest/rest.go` and `endpoints/handlers/`):\n```go\ntype Storage interface {\n    New() runtime.Object           // Return empty object\n    Destroy()                      // Clean up on shutdown\n}\n\ntype Creater interface {\n    Storage\n    Create(ctx, obj, createValidation, options) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n\ntype Updater interface {\n    New() runtime.Object\n    Update(ctx, name, objInfo, createValidation, updateValidation, forceAllowCreate, options) (runtime.Object, bool, error)\n}\n\n// Similar for Getter, Deleter, Lister, Watcher\n```\n\n**How to extend**:\n1. Implement the REST interfaces (Creater, Updater, Getter, etc.)\n2. Wrap with admission validation using `rest.AdmissionToValidateObjectFunc()`\n3. Register in the API group's `VersionedResourcesStorageMap`\n4. Full control over validation, transformation, and storage backend\n\n**Example**: CRD validation schema + custom validation rules via CEL.\n\n**Risk**: Custom storage can introduce performance bottlenecks (e.g., calling external APIs on every create).\n\n### 5.3 Custom Authenticators and Authorizers\n\n**Authenticator** (see `authentication/authenticator/interfaces.go`):\n```go\ntype Token interface {\n    AuthenticateToken(ctx context.Context, tokenString string) (*Response, bool, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Authorizer** (see `authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go`):\n```go\ntype Authorizer interface {\n    Authorize(ctx context.Context, a Attributes) (Decision, string, error)\n}\n```\n\n**How to extend**:\n1. Implement `Token` or `Authorizer` interfaces\n2. Register via command-line flags:\n   - `--authentication-token-webhook-config-file`\n   - `--authentication-token-webhook-cache-ttl`\n   - `--authorization-webhook-config-file`\n   - Custom implementations can be compiled into a custom kube-apiserver binary\n\n**Limitations**: Webhooks are always authenticated with mTLS. Custom implementations must be in-process (compiled into the binary).\n\n### 5.4 CustomResourceDefinitions (CRDs)\n\n**Purpose**: Define new resource types without modifying server code.\n\n**How it works** (see `ARCHITECTURE.md` L54-65):\n1. User creates a `CustomResourceDefinition` object\n2. API extensions server watches for CRDs and dynamically creates REST handlers\n3. Handlers validate objects against the CRD's OpenAPI schema\n4. Objects stored in etcd under the CRD's group/version/kind path\n\n**Advantages**: Zero downtime; no recompilation; users define schemas declaratively.\n\n**Limitations**:\n- Cannot implement custom business logic (e.g., webhook validation is separate)\n- No built-in persistence transformation layer\n- Watch cache applies globally; cannot customize per-CRD\n\n### 5.5 APIServices (Aggregated API Servers)\n\n**Purpose**: Route requests to external API servers.\n\n**How it works** (see `ARCHITECTURE.md` L33-45):\n1. User creates an `APIService` object claiming a group/version (e.g., `example.com/v1`)\n2. Aggregator server watches APIServices and proxies matching requests\n3. Requests are forwarded to a backing `Service` (resolved via `ServiceResolver`)\n4. Responses are passed through transparently\n\n**Advantages**: Full control; can implement arbitrary logic; runs in separate process.\n\n**Limitations**:\n- Requires separate deployment\n- Must handle all requests (no fallback to extensions server)\n- Watch proxying not supported\n\n**Risk**: External API server crash or slowness affects the whole cluster.\n\n### 5.6 Field Manager and Server-Side Apply\n\n**Purpose**: Track which \"manager\" (user, controller) owns each field.\n\n**Interface** (see `endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/`):\n```go\ntype FieldManager interface {\n    UpdateNoErrors(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, manager string) runtime.Object\n}\n```\n\n**How to extend**:\n- Implement the FieldManager interface to customize merge semantics\n- Called from handlers during create/update/patch operations\n\n**Customization**: By default, uses `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` library. Custom implementations can use different strategies.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications: Performance, Reliability, and Maintainability\n\n### 6.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n**Request latency drivers**:\n1. **Serialization** (~1-5ms): JSON/protobuf encode/decode of request/response\n2. **Admission webhooks** (10-100ms): External policy checks; worst case: timeout (5s)\n3. **Storage operations** (1-50ms): etcd write; dominated by raft consensus latency\n4. **Cacher lookups** (<1ms): Extremely fast; in-memory hash lookups\n\n**Optimization levers**:\n- **Batch API** (e.g., POST with multiple objects): Reduces connection overhead\n- **Cacher tuning**: `--watch-cache=true` (default) dramatically improves list/watch latency\n- **Etcd backend tuning**: SSD storage, network latency between nodes critical\n- **Admission webhooks**: Use timeout budgets; disable non-critical webhooks\n- **Request filtering**: Use label/field selectors in LIST requests to reduce memory/CPU\n\n**Metrics to watch**:\n- `apiserver_request_duration_seconds`: Request latency histogram per verb/resource\n- `apiserver_current_inflight_requests`: In-flight request count\n- `apiserver_admission_webhook_admission_duration_seconds`: Webhook latency\n- `etcd_server_slow_apply_total`: Etcd operations taking >100ms\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Failure Recovery\n\n**Failure modes and recovery**:\n\n| Failure | Symptom | Recovery |\n|---------|---------|----------|\n| Etcd down | All writes rejected; reads from cache still work | Restart etcd; API server will reconnect automatically |\n| Etcd leader election | Writes briefly stall (~1s) | Automatic; raft consensus handles |\n| Admission webhook crashes | Requests hang or rejected (if fail-closed) | Disable webhook; restart; check webhook logs |\n| API server memory leak | OOM killer terminates server | Restart; investigate cacher memory usage or leaked goroutines |\n| High CPU (watch cache churn) | Slow LIST/WATCH responses | Reduce number of resources; use namespaces for isolation |\n\n**High availability setup**:\n- Run 3+ API server replicas behind a load balancer\n- Each replica connects to the same etcd cluster\n- Requests are load-balanced (no session affinity needed)\n- Leader election not required (stateless design)\n\n### 6.3 Maintainability and Operational Burden\n\n**Key operational considerations**:\n\n1. **Configuration complexity**: `kube-apiserver` accepts 100+ flags (authentication, authorization, admission, encryption, audit, etc.). Misconfigurations are common.\n\n2. **Admission webhook management**: Over time, webhooks accumulate. Each adds latency and failure risk. Audit and clean up unused webhooks.\n\n3. **Audit logging overhead**: Audit log volume can be 1GB+/hour in large clusters. Consider log filtering and log rotation carefully.\n\n4. **Encryption key rotation**: Encryption keys are persisted in etcd. Rotation requires reading all data, re-encrypting, and writing back. Plan for downtime.\n\n5. **API deprecation**: Older API versions must be supported for backward compatibility. Removing versions requires careful planning and communication.\n\n6. **Custom resources proliferation**: Every CRD adds watch cache memory overhead. Monitor CRD count and consider limits.\n\n**Operational best practices**:\n- Monitor apiserver metrics continuously (prometheus + alerting)\n- Use dry-run mode for admission policies before production deployment\n- Test failover scenarios (etcd node failures, API server restarts)\n- Document custom admission policies and their business impact\n- Regularly review and prune unused resources (old API versions, webhooks, etc.)\n- Use RBAC to audit who is modifying API server configuration\n\n### 6.4 Debugging and Troubleshooting\n\n**Available debug tools**:\n\n| Tool | Purpose | Access |\n|------|---------|--------|\n| `--v=4` | Klog verbosity level | Command-line flag |\n| `--audit-policy-file` | Per-request audit logging | File-based configuration |\n| `/metrics` | Prometheus metrics | HTTP endpoint (usually secured) |\n| `pprof` debug socket | CPU/memory profiling | Unix socket at `--debug-socket-path` |\n| `/debug/flags` | View/modify feature gates at runtime | Unprotected HTTP endpoint |\n| `/openapi/v3` | OpenAPI schema for all resources | HTTP endpoint |\n| `--enable-priority-and-fairness-logging` | Track request scheduling | Command-line flag |\n\n**Common debugging scenarios**:\n\n1. **Request stuck/slow**:\n   - Check `apiserver_current_inflight_requests` metric\n   - Look for slow admission webhooks in logs (`--v=4`)\n   - Check etcd latency: `etcd_server_slow_apply_total`\n\n2. **Watch stream disconnected**:\n   - Check if cacher's watch history window expired\n   - Verify etcd health (leadership, storage, network)\n   - Increase `--watch-cache-sizes` if high-frequency resource\n\n3. **Admission webhook rejecting valid requests**:\n   - Test webhook with dry-run first\n   - Check webhook server logs (external to API server)\n   - Temporarily disable webhook to isolate issue\n\n---\n\n## 7. Important Files and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `pkg/server/config.go` | Config struct, handler chain builder (`DefaultBuildHandlerChain`) |\n| `pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` | Main GenericAPIServer runtime; API group registration |\n| `pkg/endpoints/installer.go` | REST route installation; URL to handler mapping |\n| `pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go` | POST request handling; admission invocation flow |\n| `pkg/endpoints/handlers/get.go` | GET request handling; response serialization |\n| `pkg/endpoints/handlers/watch.go` | Watch request handling; stream upgrades |\n| `pkg/admission/interfaces.go` | Admission plugin interfaces (MutationInterface, ValidationInterface) |\n| `pkg/admission/plugins.go` | Built-in admission plugin registry |\n| `pkg/authentication/authenticator/interfaces.go` | Token authenticator interface |\n| `pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go` | Authorizer interface |\n| `pkg/storage/interfaces.go` | Storage.Interface and options |\n| `pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go` | In-memory watch cache implementation |\n| `pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go` | Etcd v3 backend storage implementation |\n| `pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go` | genericregistry.Store; wraps storage with REST adapter |\n| `pkg/util/flowcontrol/` | Priority and Fairness (request queue management) |\n| `pkg/audit/` | Audit logging policy and event recording |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Design Tradeoffs Summary\n\n| Tradeoff | Choice | Rationale |\n|----------|--------|-----------|\n| **Optimistic concurrency** | No server-side locking | Scales better; simpler design; requires client retry logic |\n| **Watch cache** | In-memory buffer of events | Dramatically reduces etcd load; adds memory overhead; can expire if events old |\n| **Admission before deserialization** | No, after auth/authz | Saves CPU parsing untrusted requests; makes admission access to full object |\n| **Request timeouts** | Context-based, not HTTP | Prevents slow clients from blocking; allows operation to complete async |\n| **Plugin architecture** | Webhooks for extensibility | Dynamic (no recompile); adds latency and failure risk; not strongly typed |\n| **Storage backends** | Pluggable (etcd, etc.) | Allows experimentation; in practice, only etcd is production-ready |\n| **API versioning** | Multiple in-flight versions | Backward compat; complicates conversion logic; adds server memory/CPU |\n\n---\n\n## 9. Conclusion\n\nThe Kubernetes API server library is a sophisticated, production-grade framework for building REST APIs with strong consistency guarantees, security, policy enforcement, and scalability. Its architecture balances simplicity (stateless servers, no leases) with performance (watch caching) and flexibility (pluggable authentication, authorization, admission).\n\n**Key insights**:\n\n1. **Request isolation**: Each request is independent; no shared state between servers.\n2. **Admission is the main hook**: Most customization happens via admission webhooks or plugins.\n3. **Cacher is critical**: Watch cache is the secret weapon that makes Kubernetes scalable.\n4. **Etcd is the source of truth**: All durability guarantees depend on etcd correctness.\n5. **Operational complexity**: Many knobs and plugins; requires careful tuning and monitoring.\n\nFor teams building Kubernetes-like systems or extensions, the library is well-designed for reuse. The main challenges are understanding the complex request flow, debugging distributed issues, and managing the operational burden of production deployments.\n",
